<p>The <b>United States Environmental Protection Agency</b><sup id="cite_ref-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2">[2]</a></sup> (<b>EPA</b> or sometimes <b>USEPA</b>) is an <a href="/wiki/List_of_United_States_federal_agencies" class="mw-redirect" title="List of United States federal agencies">agency</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Federal_government_of_the_United_States" title="Federal government of the United States">Federal government of the United States</a> which was created for the purpose of protecting <a href="/wiki/Human_health" class="mw-redirect" title="Human health">human health</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Environmental_protection" title="Environmental protection">environment</a> by writing and enforcing regulations based on laws passed by <a href="/wiki/United_States_Congress" title="United States Congress">Congress</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-3">[3]</a></sup> The EPA was proposed by President <a href="/wiki/Richard_Nixon" title="Richard Nixon">Richard Nixon</a> and began operation on December 2, 1970, after Nixon signed an <a href="/wiki/Executive_order" class="mw-redirect" title="Executive order">executive order</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Reorganization_Plan_No._3" title="Reorganization Plan No. 3">order establishing the EPA</a> was ratified by committee hearings in the House and Senate.<sup id="cite_ref-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-4">[4]</a></sup> The agency is led by its <a href="/wiki/Administrator_of_the_Environmental_Protection_Agency" title="Administrator of the Environmental Protection Agency">Administrator</a>, who is appointed by the <a href="/wiki/President_of_the_United_States" title="President of the United States">president</a> and approved by Congress. The current administrator is <a href="/wiki/Scott_Pruitt" title="Scott Pruitt">Scott Pruitt</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-5">[5]</a></sup> The EPA is not a <a href="/wiki/Cabinet_of_the_United_States" title="Cabinet of the United States">Cabinet</a> department, but the administrator is normally given <a href="/wiki/Cabinet_of_the_United_States#Cabinet-level_officials" title="Cabinet of the United States">cabinet rank</a>.</p>
<p>The EPA has its headquarters in <a href="/wiki/Washington,_D.C." title="Washington, D.C.">Washington, D.C.</a>, regional offices for each of the agency's ten <a href="#EPA_regions">regions</a>, and 27 laboratories. The agency conducts environmental assessment, research, and education. It has the responsibility of maintaining and enforcing national standards under a variety of environmental laws, in consultation with state, tribal, and local governments. It delegates some permitting, monitoring, and enforcement responsibility to <a href="/wiki/U.S._state" title="U.S. state">U.S. states</a> and the <a href="/wiki/List_of_federally_recognized_tribes" title="List of federally recognized tribes">federally recognized tribes</a>. EPA enforcement powers include fines, <a href="/wiki/Sanctions_(law)" title="Sanctions (law)">sanctions</a>, and other measures. The agency also works with industries and all levels of government in a wide variety of voluntary pollution prevention programs and energy conservation efforts.</p>
<p>In 2016, the agency had 15,376 full-time employees.<sup id="cite_ref-EPA.27s_Budget_and_Spending_1-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EPA.27s_Budget_and_Spending-1">[1]</a></sup> More than half of EPA's employees are engineers, scientists, and environmental protection specialists; other employees include legal, public affairs, financial, and information technologists.</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=United_States_Environmental_Protection_Agency&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:BURNING_DISCARDED_AUTOMOBILE_BATTERIES._(FROM_THE_SITES_EXHIBITION._FOR_OTHER_IMAGES_IN_THIS_ASSIGNMENT,_SEE_FICHE..._-_NARA_-_553841.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/69/BURNING_DISCARDED_AUTOMOBILE_BATTERIES._%28FROM_THE_SITES_EXHIBITION._FOR_OTHER_IMAGES_IN_THIS_ASSIGNMENT%2C_SEE_FICHE..._-_NARA_-_553841.jpg/220px-BURNING_DISCARDED_AUTOMOBILE_BATTERIES._%28FROM_THE_SITES_EXHIBITION._FOR_OTHER_IMAGES_IN_THIS_ASSIGNMENT%2C_SEE_FICHE..._-_NARA_-_553841.jpg" width="220" height="149" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/69/BURNING_DISCARDED_AUTOMOBILE_BATTERIES._%28FROM_THE_SITES_EXHIBITION._FOR_OTHER_IMAGES_IN_THIS_ASSIGNMENT%2C_SEE_FICHE..._-_NARA_-_553841.jpg/330px-BURNING_DISCARDED_AUTOMOBILE_BATTERIES._%28FROM_THE_SITES_EXHIBITION._FOR_OTHER_IMAGES_IN_THIS_ASSIGNMENT%2C_SEE_FICHE..._-_NARA_-_553841.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/69/BURNING_DISCARDED_AUTOMOBILE_BATTERIES._%28FROM_THE_SITES_EXHIBITION._FOR_OTHER_IMAGES_IN_THIS_ASSIGNMENT%2C_SEE_FICHE..._-_NARA_-_553841.jpg/440px-BURNING_DISCARDED_AUTOMOBILE_BATTERIES._%28FROM_THE_SITES_EXHIBITION._FOR_OTHER_IMAGES_IN_THIS_ASSIGNMENT%2C_SEE_FICHE..._-_NARA_-_553841.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3000" data-file-height="2034" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:BURNING_DISCARDED_AUTOMOBILE_BATTERIES._(FROM_THE_SITES_EXHIBITION._FOR_OTHER_IMAGES_IN_THIS_ASSIGNMENT,_SEE_FICHE..._-_NARA_-_553841.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Stacks emitting smoke from burning discarded automobile batteries, photo taken in Houston in 1972 by <a href="/w/index.php?title=Marc_St._Gil&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Marc St. Gil (page does not exist)">Marc St. Gil</a><span class="noprint" style="font-size:85%; font-style: normal;">&#160;(<a href="https://cs.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marc_St._Gil" class="extiw" title="cs:Marc St. Gil">cs</a>)</span>, official photographer of recently founded EPA</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:SMOKESTACKS_OF_THE_HOLMES_ROAD_INCINERATOR,_NO_LONGER_POLLUTE_THE_ATMOSPHERE._THE_PLANT_PREVIOUSLY_BURNED_OLD..._-_NARA_-_557411.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c5/SMOKESTACKS_OF_THE_HOLMES_ROAD_INCINERATOR%2C_NO_LONGER_POLLUTE_THE_ATMOSPHERE._THE_PLANT_PREVIOUSLY_BURNED_OLD..._-_NARA_-_557411.jpg/220px-SMOKESTACKS_OF_THE_HOLMES_ROAD_INCINERATOR%2C_NO_LONGER_POLLUTE_THE_ATMOSPHERE._THE_PLANT_PREVIOUSLY_BURNED_OLD..._-_NARA_-_557411.jpg" width="220" height="326" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c5/SMOKESTACKS_OF_THE_HOLMES_ROAD_INCINERATOR%2C_NO_LONGER_POLLUTE_THE_ATMOSPHERE._THE_PLANT_PREVIOUSLY_BURNED_OLD..._-_NARA_-_557411.jpg/330px-SMOKESTACKS_OF_THE_HOLMES_ROAD_INCINERATOR%2C_NO_LONGER_POLLUTE_THE_ATMOSPHERE._THE_PLANT_PREVIOUSLY_BURNED_OLD..._-_NARA_-_557411.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c5/SMOKESTACKS_OF_THE_HOLMES_ROAD_INCINERATOR%2C_NO_LONGER_POLLUTE_THE_ATMOSPHERE._THE_PLANT_PREVIOUSLY_BURNED_OLD..._-_NARA_-_557411.jpg/440px-SMOKESTACKS_OF_THE_HOLMES_ROAD_INCINERATOR%2C_NO_LONGER_POLLUTE_THE_ATMOSPHERE._THE_PLANT_PREVIOUSLY_BURNED_OLD..._-_NARA_-_557411.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2026" data-file-height="3000" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:SMOKESTACKS_OF_THE_HOLMES_ROAD_INCINERATOR,_NO_LONGER_POLLUTE_THE_ATMOSPHERE._THE_PLANT_PREVIOUSLY_BURNED_OLD..._-_NARA_-_557411.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Same smokestacks in 1975 after the plant was closed in a push for greater environmental protection</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Beginning in the late 1950s<sup id="cite_ref-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-6">[6]</a></sup> and through the 1960s, Congress reacted to increasing public concern about the impact that human activity could have on the environment: the <a href="/w/index.php?title=Resources_and_Conservation_Act_of_1959&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Resources and Conservation Act of 1959 (page does not exist)">Resources and Conservation Act of 1959</a> was introduced by Senator <a href="/wiki/James_E._Murray" title="James E. Murray">James E. Murray</a> in the <a href="/wiki/86th_United_States_Congress" title="86th United States Congress">86th Congress</a>. In the years following, similar bills were introduced and hearings were held to discuss the state of the environment and Congress's potential responses. In 1968, a joint House-Senate colloquium was convened by the chairmen of the Senate Committee on Interior and Insular Affairs Senator <a href="/wiki/Henry_M._Jackson" title="Henry M. Jackson">Henry M. Jackson</a> and the House Committee on Science and Astronautics (Representative <a href="/wiki/George_Miller_(California_politician)" title="George Miller (California politician)">George Miller</a>) to discuss the need for and means of implementing a national environmental policy. In the colloquium, some Members of Congress expressed a continuing concern over federal agency actions affecting the environment.<sup id="cite_ref-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-7">[7]</a></sup></p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/National_Environmental_Policy_Act" title="National Environmental Policy Act">National Environmental Policy Act of 1969</a> (NEPA, 42 U.S.C. §§ 4321–4347)<sup id="cite_ref-Scoop_8-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Scoop-8">[8]</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template noprint Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:NOTRS" class="mw-redirect" title="Wikipedia:NOTRS"><span title="This claim needs references to better sources. (March 2013)">better&#160;source&#160;needed</span></a></i>]</sup>.<sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9">[9]</a></sup> was modeled on RCA.<sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10">[10]</a></sup> That bill would have established an Council on Environmental Quality in the office of the President, declared a national environmental policy, and required the preparation of an annual environmental report.<sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11">[11]</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template noprint Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:NOTRS" class="mw-redirect" title="Wikipedia:NOTRS"><span title="This claim needs references to better sources. (December 2012)">better&#160;source&#160;needed</span></a></i>]</sup> NEPA was declared,<sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12">[12]</a></sup> and President Nixon signed it into law on January 1, 1970. NEPA created a Council on Environmental Quality (CEQ) in the <a href="/wiki/Executive_Office_of_the_President_of_the_United_States" class="mw-redirect" title="Executive Office of the President of the United States">Executive Office of the President</a>.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (December 2012)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> NEPA required that a detailed statement of environmental impacts be prepared for all major federal actions significantly affecting the environment. The "detailed statement" would ultimately be referred to as an <a href="/wiki/Environmental_impact_statement" title="Environmental impact statement">environmental impact statement</a> (EIS).</p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:William_Ruckelshaus_Swearing_In_as_EPA_Administrator.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f1/William_Ruckelshaus_Swearing_In_as_EPA_Administrator.jpg/220px-William_Ruckelshaus_Swearing_In_as_EPA_Administrator.jpg" width="220" height="142" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f1/William_Ruckelshaus_Swearing_In_as_EPA_Administrator.jpg/330px-William_Ruckelshaus_Swearing_In_as_EPA_Administrator.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f1/William_Ruckelshaus_Swearing_In_as_EPA_Administrator.jpg/440px-William_Ruckelshaus_Swearing_In_as_EPA_Administrator.jpg 2x" data-file-width="981" data-file-height="632" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:William_Ruckelshaus_Swearing_In_as_EPA_Administrator.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Ruckelshaus sworn in as first EPA Administrator.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In 1970, President Richard Nixon proposed an executive reorganization that consolidated many environmental responsibilities of the federal government under one agency, a new Environmental Protection Agency. House and Senate reviewed and passed the proposal.<sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13">[13]</a></sup></p>
<p>Staff recall that in the early days there was "an enormous sense of purpose and excitement" and the expectation that “there was this agency which was going to do something about a problem that clearly was on the minds of a lot of people in this country,” leading to tens of thousands of resumes from those eager to participate in the mighty effort to clean up America’s environment.<sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14">[14]</a></sup></p>
<p>When EPA first began, the private sector felt strongly that the environmental protection movement was a passing fad, and the agency’s first administrator, <a href="/wiki/William_Ruckelshaus" title="William Ruckelshaus">William Ruckelshaus</a>, felt pressure to show a public which was deeply skeptical about government’s effectiveness, that EPA could respond effectively to widespread concerns about pollution.<sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15">[15]</a></sup></p>
<p>The EPA began regulating <a href="/wiki/Greenhouse_gases" class="mw-redirect" title="Greenhouse gases">greenhouse gases</a> (GHGs) from mobile and stationary sources of air pollution under the <a href="/wiki/Clean_Air_Act_(United_States)" title="Clean Air Act (United States)">Clean Air Act (CAA)</a> for the first time on January 2, 2011. Standards for mobile sources have been established pursuant to Section 202 of the CAA, and GHGs from stationary sources are controlled under the authority of Part C of Title I of the Act per <a href="/wiki/Regulation_of_Greenhouse_Gases_Under_the_Clean_Air_Act" class="mw-redirect" title="Regulation of Greenhouse Gases Under the Clean Air Act">Regulation of Greenhouse Gases Under the Clean Air Act</a>.</p>
<p>In May 2013, Congress renamed the EPA headquarters as the <a href="/wiki/William_Jefferson_Clinton_Federal_Building" title="William Jefferson Clinton Federal Building">William Jefferson Clinton Federal Building</a>, after former president <a href="/wiki/Bill_Clinton" title="Bill Clinton">Bill Clinton</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">[16]</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Writing_better_articles#Stay_on_topic" title="Wikipedia:Writing better articles"><span title="The material near this tag may contain information that is not relevant to the article's main topic. (March 2017)">relevant?</span></a> <span class="metadata">– <a href="/wiki/Talk:United_States_Environmental_Protection_Agency" title="Talk:United States Environmental Protection Agency">discuss</a></span></i>]</sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Organization">Organization</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=United_States_Environmental_Protection_Agency&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Organization">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>The EPA is led by an <a href="/wiki/Administrator_of_the_Environmental_Protection_Agency" title="Administrator of the Environmental Protection Agency">Administrator of the Environmental Protection Agency</a>. As of 2017<sup class="plainlinks noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=United_States_Environmental_Protection_Agency&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Scott_Pruitt" title="Scott Pruitt">Scott Pruitt</a> is the 14th administrator.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Offices">Offices</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=United_States_Environmental_Protection_Agency&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Offices">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<ul>
<li>Office of the Administrator (OA)<sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">[17]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">[18]</a></sup></li>
<li>Office of Administration and Resources Management (OARM)<sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19">[19]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20">[20]</a></sup></li>
<li>Office of Air and Radiation (OAR)<sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21">[21]</a></sup></li>
<li>Office of Chemical Safety and Pollution Prevention (OCSPP)<sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22">[22]</a></sup></li>
<li>Office of the Chief Financial Officer (OCFO)<sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23">[23]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Office_of_Enforcement_and_Compliance_Assurance" title="Office of Enforcement and Compliance Assurance">Office of Enforcement and Compliance Assurance</a> (OECA)<sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24">[24]</a></sup></li>
<li>Office of Environmental Information (OEI)<sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">[25]</a></sup></li>
<li>Office of General Counsel (OGC)<sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">[26]</a></sup></li>
<li>Office of <a href="/wiki/Inspector_general#United_States" title="Inspector general">Inspector General</a> (OIG)<sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27">[27]</a></sup></li>
<li>Office of International and Tribal Affairs (OITA)<sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">[28]</a></sup></li>
<li>Office of Research and Development (ORD)<sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29">[29]</a></sup></li>
<li>Office of Land and Emergency Management (OLEM)<sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">[30]</a></sup></li>
<li>Office of Water (OW)<sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31">[31]</a></sup></li>
</ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Regions">Regions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=United_States_Environmental_Protection_Agency&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Regions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Regions_of_the_United_States_EPA.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cf/Regions_of_the_United_States_EPA.svg/220px-Regions_of_the_United_States_EPA.svg.png" width="220" height="136" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cf/Regions_of_the_United_States_EPA.svg/330px-Regions_of_the_United_States_EPA.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cf/Regions_of_the_United_States_EPA.svg/440px-Regions_of_the_United_States_EPA.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="959" data-file-height="593" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Regions_of_the_United_States_EPA.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The administrative regions of the United States Environmental Protection Agency.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Creating 10 EPA regions was an initiative that came from President Richard Nixon.<sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32">[32]</a></sup></p>
<p>Each EPA regional office is responsible within its states for implementing the Agency's programs, except those programs that have been specifically delegated to states.</p>
<ul>
<li>Region 1: responsible within the states of <a href="/wiki/Connecticut" title="Connecticut">Connecticut</a>, <a href="/wiki/Maine" title="Maine">Maine</a>, <a href="/wiki/Massachusetts" title="Massachusetts">Massachusetts</a>, <a href="/wiki/New_Hampshire" title="New Hampshire">New Hampshire</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rhode_Island" title="Rhode Island">Rhode Island</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Vermont" title="Vermont">Vermont</a> (<a href="/wiki/New_England" title="New England">New England</a>).</li>
<li>Region 2: responsible within the states of <a href="/wiki/New_Jersey" title="New Jersey">New Jersey</a> and <a href="/wiki/New_York_(state)" class="mw-redirect" title="New York (state)">New York</a>. It is also responsible for the US territories of <a href="/wiki/Puerto_Rico" title="Puerto Rico">Puerto Rico</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/U.S._Virgin_Islands" class="mw-redirect" title="U.S. Virgin Islands">U.S. Virgin Islands</a>.</li>
<li>Region 3: responsible within the states of <a href="/wiki/Delaware" title="Delaware">Delaware</a>, <a href="/wiki/Maryland" title="Maryland">Maryland</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pennsylvania" title="Pennsylvania">Pennsylvania</a>, <a href="/wiki/Virginia" title="Virginia">Virginia</a>, <a href="/wiki/West_Virginia" title="West Virginia">West Virginia</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/District_of_Columbia" class="mw-redirect" title="District of Columbia">District of Columbia</a>.</li>
<li>Region 4: responsible within the states of <a href="/wiki/Alabama" title="Alabama">Alabama</a>, <a href="/wiki/Florida" title="Florida">Florida</a>, <a href="/wiki/Georgia_(U.S._state)" title="Georgia (U.S. state)">Georgia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kentucky" title="Kentucky">Kentucky</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mississippi" title="Mississippi">Mississippi</a>, <a href="/wiki/North_Carolina" title="North Carolina">North Carolina</a>, <a href="/wiki/South_Carolina" title="South Carolina">South Carolina</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Tennessee" title="Tennessee">Tennessee</a>.</li>
<li>Region 5: responsible within the states of <a href="/wiki/Illinois" title="Illinois">Illinois</a>, <a href="/wiki/Indiana" title="Indiana">Indiana</a>, <a href="/wiki/Michigan" title="Michigan">Michigan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Minnesota" title="Minnesota">Minnesota</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ohio" title="Ohio">Ohio</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Wisconsin" title="Wisconsin">Wisconsin</a>.</li>
<li>Region 6: responsible within the states of <a href="/wiki/Arkansas" title="Arkansas">Arkansas</a>, <a href="/wiki/Louisiana" title="Louisiana">Louisiana</a>, <a href="/wiki/New_Mexico" title="New Mexico">New Mexico</a>, <a href="/wiki/Oklahoma" title="Oklahoma">Oklahoma</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Texas" title="Texas">Texas</a>.</li>
<li>Region 7: responsible within the states of <a href="/wiki/Iowa" title="Iowa">Iowa</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kansas" title="Kansas">Kansas</a>, <a href="/wiki/Missouri" title="Missouri">Missouri</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Nebraska" title="Nebraska">Nebraska</a>.</li>
<li>Region 8: responsible within the states of <a href="/wiki/Colorado" title="Colorado">Colorado</a>, <a href="/wiki/Montana" title="Montana">Montana</a>, <a href="/wiki/North_Dakota" title="North Dakota">North Dakota</a>, <a href="/wiki/South_Dakota" title="South Dakota">South Dakota</a>, <a href="/wiki/Utah" title="Utah">Utah</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Wyoming" title="Wyoming">Wyoming</a>.</li>
<li>Region 9: responsible within the states of <a href="/wiki/Arizona" title="Arizona">Arizona</a>, <a href="/wiki/California" title="California">California</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hawaii" title="Hawaii">Hawaii</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nevada" title="Nevada">Nevada</a>, the territories of <a href="/wiki/Guam" title="Guam">Guam</a> and <a href="/wiki/American_Samoa" title="American Samoa">American Samoa</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Navajo_Nation" title="Navajo Nation">Navajo Nation</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">[33]</a></sup></li>
<li>Region 10: responsible within the states of <a href="/wiki/Alaska" title="Alaska">Alaska</a>, <a href="/wiki/Idaho" title="Idaho">Idaho</a>, <a href="/wiki/Oregon" title="Oregon">Oregon</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Washington_(state)" title="Washington (state)">Washington</a>.</li>
</ul>
<p>Each regional office also implements programs on <a href="/wiki/List_of_Indian_reservations_in_the_United_States" title="List of Indian reservations in the United States">Indian Tribal lands</a>, except those programs delegated to tribal authorities.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Related_legislation">Related legislation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=United_States_Environmental_Protection_Agency&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Related legislation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>The laws below are general environmental protection measures, and may also apply to other units of the government, including the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Department_of_the_Interior" title="United States Department of the Interior">Department of the Interior</a> and the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Department_of_Agriculture" title="United States Department of Agriculture">Department of Agriculture</a>.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Air">Air</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=United_States_Environmental_Protection_Agency&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Air">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<ul>
<li>1955: <a href="/wiki/Air_Pollution_Control_Act" title="Air Pollution Control Act">Air Pollution Control Act</a> PL 84-159</li>
<li>1963: <a href="/wiki/Clean_Air_Act_(United_States)" title="Clean Air Act (United States)">Clean Air Act</a> PL 88-206</li>
<li>1965: <a href="/wiki/Motor_Vehicle_Air_Pollution_Control_Act" class="mw-redirect" title="Motor Vehicle Air Pollution Control Act">Motor Vehicle Air Pollution Control Act</a> PL 89-272</li>
<li>1966: <a href="/wiki/Clean_Air_Act_Amendments" class="mw-redirect" title="Clean Air Act Amendments">Clean Air Act Amendments</a> PL 89-675</li>
<li>1967: <a href="/wiki/Air_Quality_Act" class="mw-redirect" title="Air Quality Act">Air Quality Act</a> PL 90-148</li>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Programs">Programs</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=United_States_Environmental_Protection_Agency&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Programs">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:A_BULLDOZER_PILES_BOULDERS_IN_AN_ATTEMPT_TO_PREVENT_LAKE_SHORE_EROSION_-_NARA_-_547031.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/05/A_BULLDOZER_PILES_BOULDERS_IN_AN_ATTEMPT_TO_PREVENT_LAKE_SHORE_EROSION_-_NARA_-_547031.jpg/220px-A_BULLDOZER_PILES_BOULDERS_IN_AN_ATTEMPT_TO_PREVENT_LAKE_SHORE_EROSION_-_NARA_-_547031.jpg" width="220" height="153" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/05/A_BULLDOZER_PILES_BOULDERS_IN_AN_ATTEMPT_TO_PREVENT_LAKE_SHORE_EROSION_-_NARA_-_547031.jpg/330px-A_BULLDOZER_PILES_BOULDERS_IN_AN_ATTEMPT_TO_PREVENT_LAKE_SHORE_EROSION_-_NARA_-_547031.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/05/A_BULLDOZER_PILES_BOULDERS_IN_AN_ATTEMPT_TO_PREVENT_LAKE_SHORE_EROSION_-_NARA_-_547031.jpg/440px-A_BULLDOZER_PILES_BOULDERS_IN_AN_ATTEMPT_TO_PREVENT_LAKE_SHORE_EROSION_-_NARA_-_547031.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3000" data-file-height="2080" /></a>
